text:
This turned out a little too "dark chocolate" for me.  I learned quickly if the mixture is not timed carefully and it boils in the microwave, you will end up with a grainy texture.  I remade it with milk chocolate chips and walnuts, it was wonderful.  I sprayed the pan with oil, lined it with foil, coated that in butter and then poured in the mixture.  When cooled, I pulled the foil right out, put it on the cutting board and used the pizza cutter to make perfect squares.  I took the so-so first batch to work and kept the 2nd for myself.  :)

text:
I just had to update my review.  I've been making this recipe for a couple of years now, and just want to share a couple of my favorite variations.  I half the completed mixture prior to adding the nuts, then in half the batch I add coconut either 1/2 cup to 1 cup (the more you put in, the more it tastes like an almond joy), and the other half I'll put half the nuts and a handful of chopped candied cherries.  So good!

text:
This is such an easy and great tasting fudge recipe. To make it easier, I lined the 8X8 dish with aluminum foil. That way, when the fugde has hardened, you can lift it straight up out of the baking dish, and makes for easier cutting. Also, be sure to press melted chocolate down in dish. My fudge came out with some air bubbles. Still tasted awesome though.

text:
Great, easy fudge recipe.  To prevent a grainy texture, pre-melt the butter, then add the chips and milk, stir, then microwave for 30 second intervals and keep stirring.  Takes 3 minutes to make, max!!!

text:
Wow, this is SO much better than it has any right to be! Is it exactly the same as classic double-boiler-and-candy-thermometer fudge? Not quite, but it's delicious and foolproof...and you can go from the idea of fudge to a tray cooling in your fridge in 10 minutes flat. 2 important tips:

1. Use salted butter. That pinch of salt is essential to the flavor balance.

2. The fudge will only be as good as the chocolate you use. Pay the extra buck for Ghirardelli instead of Nestle and the result will be VASTLY superior.

text:
A sweet and simple recipe.  In lieu of warming the ingredients in the microwave, I melted them together in a medium saucepan over medium heat.  After pouring the fudge batter into an 8 x 8 glass baking dish, I sprinkled crushed walnuts on top (rather than mixing the nuts into the batter) and gently pressed down to adhere to the batter.  I melted additional semi sweet chocolate chips in a double boiler and drizzled the melted chocolate over the crushed walnuts to affix them to the fudge.  I think next time I will add a teaspoon of double strength vanilla extract or perhaps peppermint or orange extract for modification.

text:
Wow, talk about an easy recipe!  I have always gone through much trouble to make my fudge so I was very leary about this recipe.  After reading the reviews I decided to give it a shot.  Boy am I glad I did!  It is super easy and very tasty.  Definately creamy with no sugar grit whatsoever.  I am not a fan of dark chocolate so thanks to the reviews I changed it up a bit too.  I used 4 cups milk chocolate chips and 2 cups semi-sweet chocolate chips.  I doubled the recipe as offered by the author of this recipe and also lined my pan with foil saturated with butter.  Its a keeper!  Thank you so much for providing such a fantastic fudge recipe.  The fact that it is super easy to make is a super bonus but I would make it again if it took me all afternoon!  :)

text:
I make fudge every year for Christmas, I made this fudge for the first time last year. I received more compliments for it than any other fudge I've ever made. The recipe is very adjustable. One variation I use is to make one batch with semi sweet and one with white chocolate. I spread the semi sweet into a pan, then spoon the white chocolate on top and run a knive through the pan to create swirls. You have to microwave the batches one right after the other and be careful not to swirl the fudge too much or the two batches will blend together. I will make this fudge every year.

Made it as written the first time and as others had noted was just a bit to much chocolate.  The second time I used half milk chocolate, half semisweet  and it was awesome.  Then I made what my family now calls  "the worlds best maple nut fudge".  I used white chcolate chips and added 3 tsp of maple flavoring (Mapeline) at the end.  It is softer setting than the chocolate but still can be cut.  I might decrease the amount of butter a little bit the next time. The addition of the chopped walnuts takes it over the top. Its as good as the maple fudge that I purchase at our local candy store, where everything is homemade.  Now I am looking for peanut butter chips to make PB fudge.  Thanks Dana for posting this recipe!

I've always been afraid of making fudge, It seemed intimiating to me, but this fudge was sooo easy that I am going to put it on my Christmas candy list from now on. It tasted great too! Wonderfully rich and creamy...everything that fudge should be. I made one batch with pecans, and one with almonds (small, whole, salted) and coconut flakes (lots of them). It was great and tasted a lot like almond joy. I did line the pans with parchment paper and then after filling, put a piece of parchment on top and pressed it down good in the pan. When It was cooled, I pulled out the fudge and cut it up. easy-peasy! Thanks for the great recipe!

Great easy recipe!! My only complaint is that with semi sweet chips, it tastes like...well semi sweet chips.  I think mixing some milk chocolate and semi sweet would make it taste "fudgier"  

TIP: for all of those who say it didn't set; it means  the chocolate melted too much...if you remove the mix just as the chips melt (but still holding their "chip" shape) and then mix it...it almost sets immediately.

text:
I have made this recipe for years, and I just wanted to make one helpful comment.  Just make sure that you use a good quality brand name chocolate chip, as the cheaper store brands are just not as good.  I prefer Ghiradelli or Hersheys, but have used Toll House also.  If it is a bit too dark for some, just substitiute 1.5 c of semisweet and 1.5 c. of milk chocolate chips for the 3 c. of semisweet the recipe calls for.  Try out variations also, it is delicious!

text:
This is by far THE EASIEST recipe I have ever used for fudge.  I have made this fudge many times, with many variations on the basic recipe.  Dark chocolate, milk chocolate, white chocolate, flavored, nuts, dried fruit, coconut...works like a charm nearly every time.  I will tell you two tips: one, butterscotch chips do not make very good fudge as they don't melt the same as chocolate does, and two, green mint chips mixed with chocolate chips comes out an odd greyish-green color (though it still tastes really good).  I have added 1-2 tsp of extract (orange and raspberry are two of my favorites, and peppermint is very good too) after the mixture's done in the microwave too.

My favorite is a mix of 2 cups milk chocolate, 1 cup Hershey's Special Dark, chopped walnuts and dried cherries, and a tsp. of vanilla extract.

Let me start out by saying that I'm always a tough judge when it comes to fudge. We made this fudge for Christmas (with 2 cups milk chocolate, 1 cup semisweet) and we got rave reviews from all of our family members. Like another reviewer said, I still think it was a little too "dark", and more importantly to me, it was too hard. I prefer a softer fudge, so next time I might consider adding some whipping cream or more butter or something. That said, the hardest part of the recipe was cutting it after it was refrigerated.  Oh yeah, I don't know how big a piece of fudge these people are eating, but it can easily make 24 pieces of fudge. Maybe 32...if you want to cut that much.

Really easy. I mean REALLY easy. I have made it multiple times with multiple different flavors. Added orange extract to the chocolate. Add-ins - peppermint with candy cane chunks, crushed oreos, almonds with almond extract, heath bits, and we did one where we poured half the mixture then a layer of roasted almonds, melted caramel, and the last layer of the fudge. Very good fudge. I always do one and a half packages of chips though. One package is not firm enough. Line your dish with aluminum foil and spray it. Pops out easy to cut. A friend begged me, asking what he could do to get more fudge he loved it so much.

text:
that was so easy and delicious! i tweaked the recipe a little, to make it milk chocolate and PB. it was SO GOOD! i just split the condensed milk & butter into two different bowls, then added 1 1/2 c PB chips or milk chocolate chips to each. i microwaved 1 bowl at a time on high for 1 minute, stirred, and then poured. it turned out to be a nice layering of flavors. you do have to move fast, as it starts to harden quickly. i would heat 1 type, pour it, and then heat and pour the next flavor also, i lined the glass pan with parchment paper and lightly buttered it. this worked out great. bravo for easy & yummy!

text:
Deliciously smooth...never quite set up like I'm used to, but tasted great enough to make up for that!  I used generic store brand chips (didn't even splurge for Nestle), and didn't have any trouble with taste or waxiness.  I used 2 c. milk chocolate chips with 2/3 of the butter and condensed milk called for, microwaved them together just until melted, then stirred in ~3/4 c. chopped walnuts and 1 tsp. almond extract.  Poured it in a foil-lined, greased 9x9.  Then microwaved together 1 c. white chocolate chips with 1/3 the butter and condensed milk called for until melted, and stirred in 1 drop red food coloring, 2 drops yellow food coloring, and 1/2 tsp orange extract.  Poured it on top of the milk chocolate layer, then marbled with a knife.  Everyone loved it!  Can't wait to try an Almond Joy version...

text:
These were very easy to make and really good. They were definitely not as sweet as most fudge which is a good thing to me.  If you like really sweet fudge, substitute some or all of the semi sweet chocolate chips with milk chocolate. I only put the nuts in half of the fudge because my husband likes nuts in his while my daughter and I don't.  I made these on the stove instead of the microwave. I just melted the butter and then put the chocolate chips and sweetened condensed milk in the pan on the stove on low heat to melt the chocolate chips. It works fine that way as long as you continually stir.

text:
Fool-proof Recipe! 

I made these to give to someone else for their birthday. They loved them! People were asking for the recipe. It tastes delicious!

It was so easy! I microwaved for 3 minutes without stirring in between and put pecan pieces on top. I also made it without the butter and added a pinch of salt. They came out almost identical but I think I prefer with butter. But the two are so similar that I'm really not sure because I don't even think I can tell them apart. I put one in a 17x12(lined with greased wax paper in a metal pan) and one in an 8x8 greased glass. I lifted the wax paper off and the pieces are very thin but they cut beautifully! 

I tried to make old fashioned fudge first(with cocoa) and I ended up with ice-cream topping. I eventually want to master it but I didn't have time to mess around so I found this easy recipe and it worked like a charm but the real version would be a money-saver as well as a recipe that is easy to make with ingredients already on hand.

This is my go to fudge recipe.  It turns out better for me than the stovetop versions. It doesn't get that grainy  texture that fudge sometimes gets.  I think the trick is to stir it a couple of times during cooking and don't overcook it.  As soon as its melted, pull it out. text:
This recipe is AWESOME! I'd never made fudge before and was glad to find a recipe without marshmallow creme. I was skeptical of the microwave but it turned out perfect. I had to microwave for 6 minutes at 50% power, removing every two minutes to stir. The first day it tasted a little funky, but after two or three days the flavor mellowed out a tad and it was DELICIOUS. I also made a butterscotch fudge using the same recipe, subsituting butterscotch chips for chocolate, and 1/2 c almonds and 1/2 c pecans for the 1 c walnuts. It's a little too nutty, so I'd go a little easier on the nuts with butterscotch. I also used white chocolate chips, added 1 tsp of mint extract and crushed 12 peppermint candies to add to the mix. The flavor is wonderful, both the white chocolate and the mint are subtle, neither overwhelms the other. It could use more of the peppermint candies, though. Next up: trying peanut butter fudge using 3 c crunchy peanut butter (not chips) instead of chocolate chips. YUM!

text:
Read some of the reviews and I used a pyrex glass dish, 3 cups of milk chocolate chip, mixed the condensed milk with the chips before microwaving and put on high for 3 minutes - took out stirred and it took a minute or so to fold in the butter well. Put back on half power for one more minute just to ensure the butter was mixed in well and poured into a wax papered pyrex dish. Came out very creamy and smooth not grainy like some reviews said. It actually began to set quicker than i thought and was ready in three hours to cut. I actually think it could have been a little sweeter and will experiment, but I've had many fudge disasters in the past and this recipe as is seems to be a quick easy fool proof way to make it.

text:
I made this recipe with peanut butter chips as I didn't have enough chocolate on hand to do the whole recipe.  I thought it was okay - not like my go to fudge recipe - but I didn't have any marshmallow cream on hand.  I think that fudge is better with the marshmallow in it - it adds a lighter texture to the fudge - but this recipe is good if you want a dense, rich fudge and/or you don't have any marshmallow at the time.  I would make this again and try with the chocolate next time.  I used unsalted butter as that is what I keep on hand for baking.  I might try with salted butter next time to see if it changes the flavor much.  Overall - the easiest fudge recipe - so fast, the taste/texture - fine, but not what I am used to.

text:
I made this in four different variations, and they were all fantastic, but I improved upon them each time. The first time I followed the recipe exactly and used semi-sweet chips. Initially, I was concerned about the consistency when I did the final stir, but it came out fine. My only issue was I noticed some butter separated from the mix and pooled/congealed in air pockets on the bottom. I reduced the butter by 1 T going forward.

The second chocolate batch I used 1/2 c of peanut butter chips to cut some of the bitterness (mom's request). I added nuts this time as well. Magnificent.

The first batch of peanut butter was strictly peanut butter chips, the milk and the reduced amount of butter. Turned out great, but not as peanut buttery as I would have liked. Made another batch a few weeks later - reduced the butter to 1T and added 3T of peanut butter. It was amazing!!

Unfortunately, this recipe now gives me a super easy way to get my chocolate/sugar fix that has both a long shelf life and easy portability. I'm in trouble :)

text:
This is delectably creamy and smooth! I made this for a church function. I did double the batch and made as written except for the addition of vanilla extract as other suggested. Also, please be sure to use salted butter.  I think the taste would be blah without that bit of salt in the butter. My Mom taught me a long time ago about adding a pinch of salt to sweet stuff to enhance the flavor. I don't know why it works.  I just knows that that pinch of salts makes sweet things taste better. I put it in a 15" baking sheet (small jelly roll pan). Sprayed the pan with cooking oil then lined it with aluminum foil.  Coated the aluminum foil with butter.  I did use a 2-to-1 ratio with the chips, twice as much milk chocolate as semi-sweet.  I also used Ghirardelli milk chocolate chips but Baker semi-chocolate because I already had them on hand.  Start out with about 1 1/2 mins. in the microwave. Stir then another 1 1/2 mins.  Then carefully add additional 45 seconds to 1 minute times, stirring after each.  After the first 3 mins., start checking the true status of the "remaining" chips by squeezing one.  You'll be able to tell when those last few chips are soft enough to finish meling.  This will keep you from burning the chocolate.  I did my mixer to beat the melted chocoate for about 2 minutes.  Refrigerated overnight and then cut with a pizza cutter (what a great tip!) after removing from the pan and removing the aluminum foil.  I guess I have to agree with the comments that this d

text:
After many unsuccesful attempts at making "real" fudge...the worst being completely unedible and the best turning out as hot fudge sauce...I discovered this completely foolproof recipe.  I make it on the stove on low heat and stir until the chips are melted, then remove from heat and add a tsp of vanilla and the nuts.  Put it in a pan lined with foil and pop in the fridge. My family loves it.  I also use 2 cups of semi sweet chips and 1 cup of peanut butter chips for the best 'fudge' flavor. I can't wait to try with coconut and almonds, though.

text:
Great recipe! Simple, easy, and quick. Creamy, smooth, and delicious. I made 3 batches to give away for Christmas this year. In all the batches I took other reviewers' advice and used 1 part milk chocolate to 2 parts semi-sweet. I also doubled all three batches. The first batch I made, I messed up and did the first bit of melting on high in the microwave. It didn't seem to hurt it too badly; I added the nuts to this batch and they turned out ok. I was hoping the texture of the nuts might disguise the screw-up a little and I think it did. The next batch was plain, melted correctly, and turned out pretty well. The third batch I made, I mixed in well about 1 slight tablespoon of peppermint extract after the melting was finished. I also crushed 4 candy canes, and mixed about a teaspoon of the most finely ground powder into the fudge itself, and sprinkled the rest on top. That batch turned out the best. I saved that one covered in the refrigerator and took it to a New Year's Eve party. All the batches I made set very well in the refrigerator, and held their shape and firmness well even after being taken out of the refrigerator. I used butter flavor brand name cooking spray to coat the containers they set in and it worked like a charm. The only thing I would suggest is to cut them into very small, as in put one in your mouth at a time, pieces because they do start to melt pretty quickly once you get them in your fingers and it's a gooey mess, and a tiny bit oily from the spray. Plu

text:
No candy thermometers, no double-boilers â€” this fudge recipe is not only an easy, one-pot deal, it tastes like the stovetop stuff. I made a pan of semisweet chocolate chip-coconut stuff (used 1 cup sweetened shredded coconut in place of the nuts) and one pan of white chocolate-cranberry. The white chocolate-cranberry fudge didn't quite set properly and was a little gooey/chewy. I think this might have been because I used "real" white chocolate callets with a high percentage of cocoa butter. I think the extra sugar in chocolate chips helps the fudge to set to the proper consistency so I would stick to using chocolate chips in the recipe and not real chocolate chunks. If you do use real chocolate, consider cutting down the condensed milk a bit to help the fudge set.

text:
Easy and foolproof!  For a quick fudge fix this is awesome!  That being said, Aunt Teen's Creamy Chocolate fudge recipe on this site is the best but you have to stir forever, this is so quick, effortless, and very creamy. Thanks for the recipe, it's a keeper!  PS. Be careful not to overcook or it will turn grainy!  Update:  This is my go-to recipe when I need something quick.  I like a 1/2 and 1/2 mixture of semi-sweet and chocolate chips.  This recipe can be a little tricky if you're using a cheap microwave - my good one broke down, and the small ones are just not as good.  I would check this more closely (stop and stir more often) if you're using a microwave that is less than stellar (or doesn't give you the option to cook at a lower temp) as I mentioned before, it is easy to turn grainy.  One last tip:  butterscotch chips are WAY too sweet, best not to try that version.

text:
I took this fudge to a holiday get-together and got raves like I've never gotten before.

My variation, which tasted really deep and complex: for the three cups of chocolate, use two Hershey's Special Dark Espresso bars, broken up, plus enough semi-sweet chips to make one cup, plus one more cup of semi-sweet chips, plus a cup of milk chocolate chips. Immediately after pouring the fudge into the pan, pour about 1/2 cup of toasted chopped almonds on top, pressing down gently to get them embedded into the fudge.

The mocha taste is really divine!

text:
It's a very good recipe, my only recommendation is to use a non-stick pan on very low heat, add one can of condensed milk per each bag of chips.  I add all the milk first then the chips, constantly stirring until completely smooth.   Remove from heat and add to your preferred dish.   I've also found the best chips are Guittard Chocolate Chips, if you can find them.  See's Candies actually uses Guittard Chocolate to make their chocolates, so if you like See's you'll love Guittard chips!

text:
I have made this several times now.  The only thing I have changed is adding a teaspoon of vanilla.  To those who are having trouble with this setting up, make sure you use real butter or stick margarine.  You cannot use tub margarines or it will not set, they are too soft.  I have also added several things depending on what I want in it.  My usual addition is 1 cup of coconut and a half of cup of slivered almonds because my husband loves Almond Joys.  Have fun with this recipe and play with your additions.    To those having trouble with crystallizing, you are leaving it in the microwave too long without stirring.  If you have a 1200W microwave like I do you only need a total of 2 minutes in the micro.  Take it out and stir very well halfway through (at the one minute mark) pop it back in and finish the last minute.  It is critical that you stir it up while microwaving or it WILL crystallize every time.  Make sure you stir it very well again when you take it out.  Add your additives like coconut and nuts or dried fruits AFTER you take it out of the microwave.  So easy even a five year old can make it!

text:
I just made it using milk chocolate chips. My husband doesn't like dark chocolate, and I was also afraid the dark chocolate would be too dark chocolaty.

 I didn't use the microwave method.  I wanted to melt some marshmallows to incorporate in it (2 cups of mini marshmallows), so i made it on the stove.  I melted the butter, stirred in the marshmallows until they were melted, stirred in the sweetened condensed milk and then stirred in the chocolate until it was melted. It just took a couple of minutes. I greased a pan and then sprinkled sweetened coconut in the bottom and then poured the fudge mixture in the pan. 

It looks great,tastes fabulous!! Such a creamy texture.

text:
best, easiest fudge ever! made this for the holiday and it beat out my mom's long passed-down marshmallow creams recipe. this fudge does taste darker than other fudge, but it's good that way. I added a half tsp or so of peppermint extract which made it extra tasty. I microwaved 2 minutes at a time, stirring in between until everything was melted and combined. then I poured (plopped) it in an 8x8 pan lined with aluminum foil and refrigerated. it was set after 2-3 hours. it's kind of hard to cut when it's cold, but the consistency turned out great. very pleased...easiest fudge ever! very addictive and dangerous. :)

Made this today for an awards banquet. I used 2 cups of semi-sweet and 1 cup of milk chocolate chips (both  Ghirardelli brand. I microwaved according to directions. The batter melted well and the texture was smooth, but I was worried about hardness. The end product seemed a little soft. I sprinkled top with candy crunchies before cooling. After cooling for 2 hours in fridge I began cutting into 1 inch cubes Still seemed a little soft. I placed cubes in candy-sized paper cups and served on a tray. They disappeared over the course of the banquet, so apparently the fudge was a success.

text:
I was very impressed with this fudge!  I used salted butter and about 1 cup of semisweet and 2 cups of milk chocolate chips, and it was great.  Helpful hint:  This is great served cold, but not very good at room temperature.  Some of the negative reviews on this site say that it tasted like frosting, and I agree that this is the case when at room temperature.  However, when it was fresh out of the fridge (or even after 45 minutes of being left on the counter), it was wonderful!  I should also note that it wasn't as "fudge-like" as expected as some reviewers noted, but it was wonderful nonetheless.

text:
This was my first time making fudge. I had an idea of the great fudge my Grandmother used to make. This recipe got me about half way there. I used 2 cups white chocolate chips, 2 cups milk chocolate chips. I didn't know that the fudge needs to be "dried" after it comes out of the fridge in the morning. I suggest letting it air out another 8 hours on the counter before cutting into it if you want clean cuts/perfect squares. It had the consistency of my Grandmother's fudge but I think it does need some semi-sweet chocolate chips to make it taste more fudgey/less frosting taste.

A lot of people complained about this being rubbery or tasting like chocolate chips not fudge. I 100% believe that the quality of chocolate you use will determine the outcome. If you used cheap chips containing wax or lots of ingredients then yes itâ€™s not going to be any good. 
I used 3 ingredient real chocolate from tollhouse and real chocolate chunks from Trader Joeâ€™s, both semi sweet. USE REAL CHOCOLATE. 
Beautiful texture and taste! 

I would recommend melting the butter first, I ran into this being an issue in the microwave,  using a double boiler method instead of microwaves would probably fix a lot of this as microwaves are not an even heat. 
Otherwise fantastic recipe!

text:
This fudge was a breeze to make! We have dairy allergies in our house, so to make it dairy free I simply used coconut sweetened condensed milk and Earth Balance butter. Now, it didn't set hard. It set, but it remained soft enough where it wouldn't splinter if I cut it and it would get melty if you handled it too long. I don't know if this is because I'm making it dairy free, or if it's the recipe, or what, but if you make this dairy free, I'd make sure it was served right out of the fridge or somehow kept cool. Just to keep it firmer.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I made 2 batches of this in  1 day... it was super easy!
The first batch, was your plain jane chocolate, no nuts. It was delicious, but like other's have said, I'll probably start mixing up different types of chocolate chips to make it fudgey-ier tasting.

The second batch, I mixed 1/2 peppermint chips & 1/2 semi-sweet chips, and got a delicious fudge that tasted similar to a thin mint cookie. I have a feeling that will be one heck of a hit this holiday season. 

One last recommendation -- microwave it in 30s to 1m intervals, stirring in between each one. the first one I microwaved in 90s intervals, and by the end, it was a little "grainy" (but still tasted delicious).  It took no more than 3 minutes of microwaving for mine to be ready to pour. It was also hardened enough to be cut after just a few hours in the fridge. If you're doing a day-off holiday dessert --- this is a perfect one!!

I used 1 cup of semi sweet and 2 cups of milk ghirardelli chocolate, when I make it again I will use semi sweet ghirardelli  chocolate, I also added about a loose cup of peanut butter and the same of that marshmallow fluff stuff a splash of a good vanilla. someone also mentioned using salted butter is a must, well I never have salted butter in my house so I did use unsalted I agree some salt normally is good to balance out the chocolate so may be next time ill use a pinch but I felt mine came out just fine with unsalted. I only buttered the pan and it came out ok but this time I will use some parchment just to make life a bit easier, over all my house hold inhaled this I cant remember what old fashioned fudge tasted like to compare it to this and dont feel the need to do so what ever this is it was great. I know I did not follow your recipe to the letter but thanks so much for posting I would never had made this with out your suggestion and all the advice that followed.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is my go-to easy fudge recipe when I want to bring something homemade and don't have much time. The best part about it is the flexibility. You can make all sorts of combinations and flavors by getting different chips. The only challenge is to not ever let the chips boil or you might get a grainy fudge. Having room temperature butter or chopping cold butter into chunks will help everything come together at the same time. I check and stir every  minute. When the last of the chips are no longer visible, you are ready to pour into a buttered dish. (No veg. oil spray for taste reasons.) In my most recent batch, I got Andes mint candy chips (2 cups in bag) and added a cup of semi-sweet chips to make a mint chocolate fudge. I kept a couple tablespoons of the Andes chips out to top the fudge so people would know it was mint. I like to use a milk chocolate chip, and the better the chip quality, the better your fudge will be. I have swirled this with a microwave peanut butter fudge, and it makes a nice-looking, yummy fudge. Another tip: Add the walnuts by sprinkling them on top and slightly mashing down after you spread the fudge in the pan. You can have two kinds of fudge in one pan and make the walnut-haters happy!

text:
After reading the reviews, I made it as directed with the multiple suggestions of using half semi-sweet and half milk chocolate Ghiradelli chips. The sweetness was good. The reason I gave it 4 stars is because it was incredibly fast. You just dump everything in a bowl and microwave it (only took me 1:30 plus an additional 0:30). It will fix the craving for fudge, but I wouldn't rely on this recipe for impressing anyone. It really does just taste like softened chocolate chips. If it weren't lightning fast and easy to make, I would've only given it 3 stars but there is something to be said about a recipe that says fast and easy- and is. So if you just want a quick sweet that resembles fudge somewhat, this is your best pick. If you want something that tastes like how fudge does in your mind, you will need to find a recipe that does not say "fast and easy".

text:
Really easy recipe!  I loved that all of the ingredients were ones I normally keep in stock. 

 I opted to  put the ingredients in a saucepan on medium-low heat. The trick with this technique is to constantly stir the mixture, so that the chips don't clump together or stick to the sides of the pan. 

The aluminum foil tip seems like a good idea. However, I chose to stick with the grease method for this first batch.

This will make a perfect holiday treat.

text:
Based on comments, and wanting rich dark fudge,  I used half bittersweet & half semisweet of the best chocolate I could buy at the local gourmet grocers.  Then I changed up the technique & I will say it made for the finest fudge,  yum!
I used a double boiler method,  and melted just the chocolate slowly,  then I added in the condensed milk.  This is not easy - you really got to stir that milk into the chocolate.  I resisted the urge to increase the heat on the water. 
Then I sliced off 3 tablespoons of butter from right out the fridge,  and stirred that in - which isn't easy. Then I did it again.  By then the fudge was well mixed & real glossy & I didn't use the rest of the butter.  I added the nuts,  forgot the cherries I had intended,  and spread it into a 12 x 9 pan.  Sprinkled with some Celtic  sea salt.  So delish.

Instead of using the microwave I used a double boiler.  Melted butter, added in sweetest condensed milk, and then the chocolate.  I cooked it on low until it was thoroughly melted and mixed.  I doubled the recipe.  Made one pan w/ nuts over the top and one pan with mini chocolate chips over the top.  Of course, put in greased pans and refrigerated until ready.  They look fabulous and taste fabulous too.  Next time I'll try w/ milk chocolate and a little more sweetened condensed milk.

text:
I have made this for a few years this way now and it is the easiest fudge I have ever made. I haven't had any issues with it setting up or being grainy. I have had many, many compliments on it and am asked to make it yearly. For best results, I recommend keeping it refrigerated. I use 2 cups semi-sweet and 1 cup milk chocolate chips. It's easy and people think you spent hours on it. My 90 year old mother-in-law loves it and she used to always do it the old fashioned way with cooking, candy thermometer, etc. She can't believe I made it in the microwave. I also use the foil lined tip for easy removal.

text:
I used to make a similar simple fudge recipe for years.  Makes a nice gift for a chocoholic.  The only difference was I did not use nuts and I amped the flavor up by adding a little all natural almond extract...not too much, just a 1/2 tsp.  you can add a bit of vanilla with it.  I will say that I found the consistency to be a bit better if I melted the chocolate and butter together first, then stirred in the extracts and condensed milk after the chocolate was melted and removed from the heat immediately after everything is incorporated.

text:
I made this with my 6 year old nephew as a treat for the family, and everyone loved it. It was easy to make and tasted good. I heated the milk and butter first in the microwave, and then added the chocolate chips after (I've had bad experiences with seized chocolate!). It worked out fine, and the kids added sprinkles, mini marshmallows and m&m's on top of the fudge before it cooled. One tip, though - I lined the pan with greased foil, that way when the fudge cooled I just lifted the foil out and wrapped it around the fudge to store. Thanks for the recipe.

text:
Okay... So I just used up all my characters on this long, detailed review, and I clicked submit, and it didn't do anything. It didn't post on the site, I didn't get any notifications... So I'm guessing I just lost it :( This is definitely a crowd pleaser. People who say they don't like peanuts decide they like it when they timidly try the peanut butter fudge, everyone asks for the recipe, that kind of thing. I love sweet stuff, so the chocolate fudge I made (using semisweet chips in a half peanut butter-half chocolate batch) was a bit bland. Good, but not worth the calories. The peanut butter though... Man, that was goooooooood! Recently though, I made an insanely delicious batch of chocolate fudge. I was confused for a while but now I have a conclusion! The time that the chocolate fudge wasn't so great was when I did a half and half batch. Maybe I put more sweetened condensed milk into the peanut butter fudge than chocolate??? Well, I also have some tips: #1: If the fudge comes out kind of grainy, you might not have set the power level to medium. If you catch yourself cooking the fudge on high, take it out of the microwave, mix it up until it's smooth, set the power level on medium, and keep on cooking! #2: I would suggest a half and half recipe, because peanut butter and chocolate taste amazing together!!!! Also, the sweetness of the peanut butter fudge balances out the semi-sweet chocolate fudge.. LOVE THIS RECIPE!!!!!!!!!!!!!
Oh - and I don't put walnuts in it :)

Gloriously smooth and easy to make. Followed the recipe as written. I think I probably didn't nuke it as long in the microwave as one review warned against letting it boil. city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was so super easy to make. I've never made fudge before so I read through a lot of the bad reviews to be aware and the only thing I added was about 2 tbsp of AP flour during the cooking process.  I cooked everything in a saucepan at med-low heat, instead of microwave, so I could monitor it better.  I melted the butter, added the chocolate and when halfway melted, I added the milk. I can't have nuts so didn't add them. I continually stirred with a silicone spatula to make sure I could get all the corners (about 10 minutes total) until it was almost like a frosting consistency.  I added a tbsp of flour, mixed well, then added another to help absorb the butter and give it a little bit more "thickness". I would suggest to anyone that adding a flour is by eye to help the butter dissolve and not sit on top of the chocolate. I used a glass dish that I lined with wax paper (but sprayed with Pam just in case) because I didn't want a "tin" taste.  About 2 hours in the fridge and I flipped it over and cut with a pizza cutter into small squares.  I only left it out during a party then stored in the fridge again.  It kept it's perfect flavor and consistency for a week (we ate it all by then) and now have friends that are paying me to make some for them.  Great recipe but for those cooking fudge for the first time, go with the saucepan.

text:
Super-easy! My husband, the fudge-connoisseur apparently, was skeptical when I told him about this recipe. He said he only likes "really good" fudge. Well, this exceeded both of our expectations! I used 1/2 semi-sweet, 1/2 milk chocolate chips, and I did use Ghirardelli chips. I nuked it for exactly 3 minutes, stirred well, and poured it into a parchment paper-lined loaf pan, cooling it in the fridge for about 3 hours. Next time I will try some crushed peppermint sticks on top. My 2 1/2-year old son also loved this... Highly recommend!

text:
By far the BEST and EASIEST fudge recipe around! I literally made and passed out 20 batches of this stuff at Christmas time. Every batch different - some made w/ peanut butter chips, caramel chips, butterscotch, etc... But mostly I LOVED the ones made with MILK chocolate chips. I added everything from walnuts, pecans, almonds, coconut, marshmallows, peanuts, crushed candy canes, crushed ANDES mints, M&Ms and on and on... Somehow in such a short time I have become famous for my fudge in my small town... haha - (I wish I could take credit for it) I literally get asked a few times a week when Im making it again, and Im certainly always happy to pass the recipe along!
**update** now that it's been a decade since I first tried making this amazing fudge, I feel like I've perfected it to fit my liking - and it's a huge hit year after year! For the basic chocolate fudge I ONLY use milk chocolate chips and it just makes such an awesome creamy taste. Even though the microwave is on medium (mine is on 60%) I still open it up and give it a stir every 15 to 20 seconds and it's always super creamy and never grainy. The best is to add mini marshmallows and walnuts and pass out delicious rocky road during the holidays!!

We loved this recipe.  Made many different variations, every one turned out great.  

Faves were butterscotch, and a variation w/ cinnamon chips and dark chocolate.  (Used just a bit more than a half cup of cinnamon chips, and make up the rest w/ chocolate chips, to get three cups total.)  

Experiment -- you really can't go wrong unless you overcook it as another reviewer mentioned.  Even then, if it's grainy, it's still a rather tasty recipe!
